**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

The r/politics subreddit on Reddit is a community focused on discussing and sharing news, analysis, and commentary related to U.S. politics. It's primarily a hub for:

### Explanation of Revisions

I have refined the initial category structure to provide a more intuitive and logical organization of the day's news. The main goal was to improve clarity, reduce overlap between categories, and create a framework that is more helpful for analyzing the political landscape.

The key changes are as follows:

1.  **Consolidation of Areas:** I reduced the number of top-level areas from six to five. This creates a more streamlined, high-level overview. The original "Domestic Policy" and "Legal Affairs" areas had significant overlap and have now been merged into a single, more cohesive area: "Domestic Governance and Legal Affairs."

2.  **Reorganization of Executive Branch Coverage:** The original "The Trump Administration" area was overly broad. I have renamed it **"The Executive Branch: Actions, Controversies, and Personnel"** and restructured its topics to better distinguish between:
    *   Specific scandals (Epstein).
    *   Broader questions of governance and power (term limits, use of memos).
    *   Concrete policy directives (immigration, funding cuts).
    *   Personnel changes.
    *   The performance of new departments like DOGE.

3.  **Integration of Economic and Domestic Policy:** I moved cross-cutting issues to their most logical homes. For instance, the shutdown of the Corporation for Public Broadcasting is a specific executive action, but its primary nature is a budgetary one, so I have created a specific topic **"Federal Budget and Funding"** under "Economic Affairs" to centralize these stories. Similarly, I created a more distinct topic for **"Civil Rights, Healthcare, and Social Policy"** to house articles about DEI, gender-affirming care, and Medicaid.

4.  **Sharpened Focus on Congressional Action:** I created a specific topic, **"Congressional Actions and Partisan Debates"** under "U.S. Politics and Public Sphere." This allows for a clear separation between actions taken by the Executive branch and the legislative branch's reactions, proposals, and internal debates (e.g., the stock ban proposal, Schumer's comments on the jobs report, votes on Israel aid). This better reflects the separation of powers as covered in the news.

This revised structure provides a more balanced and analytically useful framework for categorizing the provided news articles.

**Step 3 (logic-heavy)**

Scoring: 

Some articles are better than others, with more prestigious and reliable sources, and more factual, relevant, concise titles. So, you need to give every news article an importance score, from 1 to 10, 1 as the least important, 10 as the most important. Remember to use a consistent standard across all articles. Then, considering the importance of the topic itself, and the weight of all news reports on that topic, and then give an importance score for the topic, from 1 to 10, 1 as the least important, 10 as the most important. Remember not to saturate the scale! Use "importance 10" sparingly. And then, in the same way, give an importance score for the area containing multiple topics. 

Do this consistently for all news articles, topics and areas. Please insert the importance scores into their JSON lines, by creating a value called "importance" and insert it after "title", but keep everything else untouched. Compile all your results in a simple text file (step3.txt).

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking. Please do not get into endless cycles!


====================
    Round 7
    Assistant: 
====================

Here is the analysis with importance scores assigned to each article, topic, and area, compiled into `step3.txt`.

**Methodology for Scoring:**

*   **Article Score (1-10):** Based on the source's reliability, the headline's factual nature vs. opinion, and its direct relevance to major government functions. Reports from primary sources (like `bls.gov`) or top-tier newswires (Reuters, AP, Bloomberg) on concrete events receive higher scores. Opinion pieces or articles from highly partisan sources receive lower scores.
*   **Topic Score (1-10):** A weighted average considering the importance of the underlying issue and the quantity/quality of articles covering it. A topic with multiple high-scoring articles on a critical issue (e.g., a national jobs report) will score very high.
*   **Area Score (1-10):** An aggregation of the topic scores, reflecting the overall strategic importance of the entire domain for the day's news cycle. An area containing multiple high-stakes topics will receive a top score.

The score "10" is used sparingly to denote events of the highest immediate national importance, such as a major economic downturn or a significant military deployment.

**Step 5 (writing-heavy)**

Summarizing: 

Keep all areas and topics in their original orders determined in Step 4. For each topic, write an summary paragraph as if you are doing an academic study of the headlines. Choosing your length appropriately by importance and complexity of that topic. You should learn from all the headlines, and especially the ones with high importance scores under the topic, discover their connections, and put everything into a coherent narrative, and provide citations (the IDs of news articles) for your claims. You need to cover the main ideas behind all the articles, but you don't need to cite every single of them. You only cite the meaningful, high-quality sources. You should never use overly broad, generic phrasing, which is a mistake you often make. Keep tone urgent, stick to the facts, use concrete examples, be razor sharp, be non-partisan. Do not offer policy recommendations. No editorializing or speculation — stick strictly to facts in the JSON. Sometimes there are insufficient articles and information for a specific topic. In that case, keep to what the headlines explicitly say, and explain that information is insufficient, and keep the summary brief. Do not make your own guesses to fill up the space!

**Please be super aware of the possibility of hallucinations!** That is absolutely not allowed. This is a common problem for LLMs like you. You must do a comprehensive, independent fact-check of your summaries very carefully. Every name, job title, date, event, quote, and other facts should be exactly as what you learned from the news headlines. Be fully aware that your internal knowledge base is outdated.

After your summary, paste the entire JSON lines of the news articles you cited in the summary paragraph, directly under your summaries. This is the same for all other topics under an area and also all other areas. Compile all your results in a simple text file (step5.txt). You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

**TOP-SECRET | CONGRESSIONAL DAILY BRIEFING | FOR EYES OF DEMOCRATIC & REPUBLICAN LEADERSHIP ONLY**

**DATE:** July 26, 2025
**FROM:** Office of the Chief News Analyst
**SUBJECT:** Daily Intelligence Synthesis and Crisis Report

**A. Introduction:** This briefing provides an objective, non-partisan analysis of the most critical developments over the past 24 hours, based exclusively on curated media reports. The security, economic, and political landscape is volatile. Situational awareness is paramount for coordinated leadership.

---
**Area 1: Economic Affairs: Domestic and International**

**Topic 1.1: U.S. Labor Market and Economic Performance**

The U.S. labor market is flashing clear warning signs of a significant slowdown, a development carrying immediate negative consequences for both domestic and global financial markets. The July jobs report was deeply disappointing, indicating the creation of only 73,000 new jobs, a figure that pushed the national unemployment rate to 4.2% [1]. The severity of the situation, however, lies in the stark downward revisions to previous months’ data. In a particularly "stunning" revision, the Bureau of Labor Statistics reduced one prior month's reported gain of 147,000 to a mere 14,000 [2]. Cumulatively, these revisions have erased 258,000 previously reported jobs from the national tally, painting a much weaker picture of economic performance than was previously understood [3]. This combination of weaker-than-expected job growth and the administration's new tariff announcements has been directly linked to a sell-off in both U.S. and global stock exchanges, as markets react to the dual pressures [4].

**References:**
[1] US job growth slows sharply in July; unemployment rate rises to 4.2%, https://www.reuters.com/world/us/us-job-growth-slows-sharply-july-unemployment-rate-rises-42-2025-08-01/

### 1.1. U.S. Labor Market and Economic Performance

The U.S. labor market is flashing clear warning signs of a significant slowdown, a development carrying immediate negative consequences for both domestic and global financial markets. This combination of weaker-than-expected job growth and the administration's new tariff announcements has been directly linked to a sell-off in both U.S. and global stock exchanges [5].

## 4. Domestic Governance and Legal Affairs

### 4.1. The Judiciary and Legal Challenges

The federal judiciary is reporting increased levels of hostility and harassment, which sitting judges are publicly linking to the President's rhetoric. Federal judges have detailed a rise in threats and forms of personal harassment, including "pizza doxings," which they directly attribute to President Trump's escalating public criticism of the judicial branch [1]. Simultaneously, the judiciary continues to issue rulings that directly impede the administration's agenda. One federal judge blocked an executive action that would have ended humanitarian protections for approximately 60,000 migrants from Central America and Nepal [2]. In a separate case, another federal judge issued a "blistering ruling" that harshly rebuked a new deportation plan, going so far as to accuse the administration of "perpetuating the racist theory" of population replacement [3].

### 4.2. Environmental and Climate Policy

The administration is taking a pivotal and legally contentious step to dismantle federal climate change regulations. The Environmental Protection Agency (EPA) has initiated a formal process to revoke the "Endangerment Finding." This finding is the core scientific and legal predicate that has compelled the federal government to regulate greenhouse gases for over a decade [1]. This move is seen as the central component of what one source calls "an audacious effort to destroy climate regulations" and is widely expected to trigger a major legal battle that will ultimately be decided by the Supreme Court [2].

**References:**

## 5. U.S. Politics and Public Response

### 5.1. Congressional Actions and Partisan Debates

The Senate recently defeated a key foreign policy resolution sponsored by Sen. Bernie Sanders, which aimed to block an arms sale to Israel. While the measure failed to pass, it garnered a "record number" of Democratic votes, signaling a notable and growing level of dissent on the issue within the caucus [1]. Reporting on the final tally was inconsistent, with different outlets citing either 19 Democratic senators voting against the sale [2] or 24 total senators in favor of the resolution [3]. In other legislative maneuvering, Senate Republicans reportedly pitched a proposal to their Democratic colleagues that would exempt President Trump from a congressional stock ban [4]. On the economic front, following the release of the disappointing July jobs report, Senate Minority Leader Chuck Schumer delivered a sharp rebuke, stating that the "chickens are coming home to roost" from the administration's trade war [5]. In the House, Minority Leader Hakeem Jeffries publicly accused Texas Republicans of engaging in illegal gerrymandering, stating they are attempting to "rig the congressional map" [6].

A national protest movement critical of the administration is reportedly gaining momentum and expanding its footprint.
